    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_aedefd95-431f-4181-8f95-c4eb82dca6e8'

<span id="freeTextContainer12179771468809274997">The only daughter of a prominent samurai, Mariko has always known she’d been raised for one purpose and one purpose only: to marry. Never mind her cunning, which rivals that of her twin brother, Kenshin, or her skills as an accomplished alchemist.   <span id="freeText12179771468809274997" style="display:none">The only daughter of a prominent samurai, Mariko has always known she’d been raised for one purpose and one purpose only: to marry. Never mind her cunning, which rivals that of her twin brother, Kenshin, or her skills as an accomplished alchemist. Since Mariko was not born a boy, her fate was sealed the moment she drew her first breath.<br /><br />So, at just seventeen years old, Mariko is sent to the imperial palace to meet her betrothed, a man she did not choose, for the very first time. But the journey is cut short when Mariko’s convoy is viciously attacked by the Black Clan, a dangerous group of bandits who’ve been hired to kill Mariko before she reaches the palace.<br /><br />The lone survivor, Mariko narrowly escapes to the woods, where she plots her revenge. Dressed as a peasant boy, she sets out to infiltrate the Black Clan and hunt down those responsible for the target on her back. Once she’s within their ranks, though, Mariko finds for the first time she’s appreciated for her intellect and abilities. She even finds herself falling in love—a love that will force her to question everything she’s ever known about her family, her purpose, and her deepest desires.</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12468579784545190523"><blockquote>
  <i>“Never forget, Sanada Takeo: in this forest, there is no place to hide.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>*shivers*<br/><br/>This book was just <b>pure enjoyment from start to finish.</b> Japanese mythology, samurai, crossdressing female warriors, secrets, lies AND just the right amount of sexiness. Sure, it's not a perfect book, but somewhere along the way I forgot to care.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23308087.Flame_in_the_Mist__Flame_in_the_Mist___1_' title='Flame in the Mist (Flame in the Mist, #1) by Renee Ahdieh' rel='nofollow noopener'>Flame in the Mist</a> is set in feudal Japan. I keep seeing "Mulan retelling" floating around, but even if you ignore the fact that this is set in Japan, not China, it's a bi</span>
  <span id="freeText12468579784545190523" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“Never forget, Sanada Takeo: in this forest, there is no place to hide.”</i>
</blockquote><br />*shivers*<br /><br />This book was just <b>pure enjoyment from start to finish.</b> Japanese mythology, samurai, crossdressing female warriors, secrets, lies AND just the right amount of sexiness. Sure, it's not a perfect book, but somewhere along the way I forgot to care.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23308087.Flame_in_the_Mist__Flame_in_the_Mist___1_" title="Flame in the Mist (Flame in the Mist, #1) by Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">Flame in the Mist</a> is set in feudal Japan. I keep seeing "Mulan retelling" floating around, but even if you ignore the fact that this is set in Japan, not China, it's a bit of a stretch. Mariko doesn't go to war, for herself or for anyone else. She is travelling to the imperial city of Inako when her litter is attacked by a gang known as "The Black Clan".<br /><br />Mariko survives the attack and devises a plan to infiltrate The Black Clan, disguised as a boy. However, things don't turn out exactly how she hoped they would, and Mariko finds herself a prisoner-turned-reluctant-ally. Meanwhile, Mariko's brother and badass samurai soldier, Kenshin, is determined to prove his sister is still alive, and find the criminals responsible for the attack.<br /><br />There's some bloodsucking Jubokko trees and forest spirits, plenty of <b>action</b> and <b>bloodshed</b>, even more <b>secrets</b> and <b>betrayals</b>. The more I read, the more I started to feel like no one is as they first seem, and everyone - from the emperor's royal consort to The Black Clan's leader Takeda Ranmaru - is hiding something. <br /><br />For the most part, this book is far less romantic than Ahdieh's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18798983.The_Wrath___the_Dawn__The_Wrath___the_Dawn___1_" title="The Wrath &amp; the Dawn (The Wrath &amp; the Dawn, #1) by Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wrath &amp; the Dawn</a>. Which was fine by me. And the romance that did surface was... <b>perfection</b>. I won't spoil anything but I'll just say it's one of those rare occasions where I almost felt myself swooning. Look, there's just something sexy about the whole wolf thing, 'kay? Yes, I know, I have problems.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>"A word of warning..." He bent closer. The scent of warm stone and wood smoke emanated form his skin.<br />Mariko blinked.<br />"Don't bare your neck to a wolf."</i>
</blockquote><br />See what I mean? Problems.<br /><br /><b>All of the characters were interesting to me</b>. All of them. Even side characters like Yumi, Ren and Yoshi added something important to the story. I especially loved the complexity of Kenshin's character - he is resourceful and cares deeply for his sister and Amaya, but is also a cruel warrior. I like multifaceted characters; it keeps things interesting. And I appreciated the author's decision to put the emphasis on Mariko's smarts over her strength. I like it when female heroines have skills that real world girls can relate to, and realistically aspire to.<br /><br />Another general positive-- The use of setting was fantastic. Ahdieh captured the setting well in her previous novels, and she does it again here. I personally think many authors underestimate the atmospheric power of place. Things like this:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Inako.<br />A city of a hundred arched bridges and a thousand cherry trees. A city of mud and sweat and sewage. A city of golden cranes and amber sunsets.<br />A city of secrets.</i>
</blockquote><br />I did say this wasn't a perfect book, so I'll talk about the few negatives. Mariko makes some decisions throughout that were - to put it nicely - stupid. I didn't always understand why she did things. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[For example, saving members of The Black Clan when they're supposed to be her enemies. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And would you really bring a potentially powerful weapon to a fight when you’d <i>“never had an opportunity to test it”</i>? For at least the first half of the book, I felt like Mariko's intelligence was all tell, no show. Though, admittedly, she did seem to show some ingenuity later on.<br /><br />But, you know, whatever. <b>I enjoyed this book so much</b>. I’ve come to the conclusion that Ahdieh just has that special something that draws me in, that special storytelling charisma that you can’t get from a writing class. You can learn sentence structure; you can learn metaphor; but I don't think you can learn charm. And this author has all of the charm ♥<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12468579784545190523" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2009932370" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2009932370" />
    <a title="Elena May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57120721-elena-may"><img alt="Elena May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581020130p2/57120721.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2009932370?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elena May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elena May" href="/user/show/57120721-elena-may">Elena May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2009932370" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5818969856432684930">Don’t get discouraged by my 3 stars. The book is enjoyable, and I’ll definitely read the sequel. However, if I compare it against books I’ve rated 4 stars, it doesn’t hold up.<br/><br/>But first, I have to say <b>the premise is fantastic</b>. Set in a fantasy version of feudal Japan? A girl, dressing like a boy to infiltrate a murderous gang and to spy on them? How much better could it possibly get?<br/><br/>There is a lot to like about our protagonist, Mariko. She has book smarts—inventing bombs and smoke grenades by usi</span>
  <span id="freeText5818969856432684930" style="display:none">Don’t get discouraged by my 3 stars. The book is enjoyable, and I’ll definitely read the sequel. However, if I compare it against books I’ve rated 4 stars, it doesn’t hold up.<br /><br />But first, I have to say <b>the premise is fantastic</b>. Set in a fantasy version of feudal Japan? A girl, dressing like a boy to infiltrate a murderous gang and to spy on them? How much better could it possibly get?<br /><br />There is a lot to like about our protagonist, Mariko. She has book smarts—inventing bombs and smoke grenades by using her chemistry knowledge and improvising with the limited materials she has—but when it comes to pursuing her goals and manipulating situations to her advantage, she makes quite a few messes and questionable decisions along the way. This all feels relatable and rings true given her upbringing and experience.<br /><br />Unfortunately, the plot jumps too quickly and with no logic at certain points—Mariko going from fighting for her family to actively fighting against them in a heartbeat, the clan accepting Mariko at a point when it doesn’t make any sense, etc. We also see hints of magic, but the system is completely undeveloped and unexplained. Background characters are flat. Mariko’s father, for instance—all his lines about valuing profit more than human life felt almost cartoonish. Related to the same point, the whole criticism of the feudal system felt heavy-handed and simplistic, while there was a lot of potential for nuance.<br /><br />I think <b>nuance was the one thing I really missed in this book</b>. Everything was too easy. All problems were resolved too cleanly. Everything was too black and white, almost like in a children’s book. Wouldn’t it have been more compelling if the Black Clan had really tried to assassinate Mariko, and she understood and accepted their reasons and found her place among them in spite of that? Or if Mariko’s fiancé had turned out to be a decent person, actually wanting to help her? Or at least halfway decent? As it is, there is no reason for internal conflict because all choices are way too easy. All problems come from misunderstandings, and once those are resolved, no conflict is left.<br /><br />But in spite of its drawbacks, the book is a pleasant read and I’ll check out the second installment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5818969856432684930" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Sabaa Tahir" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26226276-sabaa-tahir"><img alt="Sabaa Tahir" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389816412p2/26226276.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1787037488?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sabaa Tahir" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sabaa Tahir" href="/user/show/26226276-sabaa-tahir">Sabaa Tahir</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1787037488" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10116729946095953060">How have I not reviewed this book? FLAME IN THE MIST is the first in a new series from Renee Ahdieh and it is FANTASTIC. I adored THE WRATH AND THE DAWN, of course, and thought the story wrapped up beautifully in THE ROSE AND THE DAGGER. But to be honest, no one can live up to smart, badass Shazi, right? Right?<br/><br/>Wrong, wrong, wrong. Mariko is a smart, brave, careful, flawed and incredibly original. I wanted to take her out of the book and get her to teach me alchemy. I want her and Shazi to meet a</span>
  <span id="freeText10116729946095953060" style="display:none">How have I not reviewed this book? FLAME IN THE MIST is the first in a new series from Renee Ahdieh and it is FANTASTIC. I adored THE WRATH AND THE DAWN, of course, and thought the story wrapped up beautifully in THE ROSE AND THE DAGGER. But to be honest, no one can live up to smart, badass Shazi, right? Right?<br /><br />Wrong, wrong, wrong. Mariko is a smart, brave, careful, flawed and incredibly original. I wanted to take her out of the book and get her to teach me alchemy. I want her and Shazi to meet and bond over all the crap they have to put up with. But Mariko isn't the only incredible character. From her twin brother Kenshin, to the Emperor, to the members of the black clan, all of the characters in this book are fully developed and deeply fascinating. I needs some novellas, pronto. <br /><br />As in Renee's other books, you can expect incredible descriptions of food and clothing and people and scenery--all the lush writing that makes you feel like you are living the story. The research that went into this book was intense, and it shows. I genuinely felt like I had been dropped into Mariko's world. The pacing is non-stop--I tore through this. But my FAVORITE part of the book was the romance. Insert all the fire emojis here. <br /><br />Pre-order it, get your hands on an ARC, trade a soul or two...it's worth it for this book. Renee, you can give me book 2 now, please. <br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1860658495" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12555731028042690540">2.5ish*<br/>This is a hard one to review for a few reasons. Namely, I have such mixed feelings. A lot of people were disappointed by this book because it was advertised as a Mulan retelling but it wasn't really a Mulan retelling, and while I see that complaint you can definitely see how it was Mulan inspired, which is what the author said it was. That aside, there were certain elements of this that I loved, especially the female empowerment, but the story as a whole was a bit of a let down. Truth is </span>
  <span id="freeText12555731028042690540" style="display:none">2.5ish*<br />This is a hard one to review for a few reasons. Namely, I have such mixed feelings. A lot of people were disappointed by this book because it was advertised as a Mulan retelling but it wasn't really a Mulan retelling, and while I see that complaint you can definitely see how it was Mulan inspired, which is what the author said it was. That aside, there were certain elements of this that I loved, especially the female empowerment, but the story as a whole was a bit of a let down. Truth is I was bored most of the time, I found it really hard to motivate myself to actually finish. I thought it was just me being too busy, but it took me 3 tries to actually get through it. So unfortunately, I don't see myself continuing with the series.</span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1860658495">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_1996503210" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1996503210" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1996503210?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fairy-tale-retellings">fairy-tale-retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=feminism">feminism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mulan">mulan</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1996503210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16794123621413333491">Like many others, I went into this—<i>gorgeous, gorgeous, gorgeous</i>—novel thinking I’d be reading a retelling of Mulan, which suited me just fine. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23308087.Flame_in_the_Mist__Flame_in_the_Mist___1_' title='Flame in the Mist (Flame in the Mist, #1) by Renee Ahdieh' rel='nofollow noopener'>Flame in the Mist</a> <b>is not a fairytale</b>, however beautifully it is written. Mariko and Mulan are both intelligent women who gain strength and fierceness along their respective journeys. <br/><br/>But Mariko never goes to war—she is recruited by the dangerous ‘‘Black Clan’’. Since that doesn’t happen, she never falls in love with a captain. Plus, she doesn't fit the cr</span>
  <span id="freeText16794123621413333491" style="display:none">Like many others, I went into this—<i>gorgeous, gorgeous, gorgeous</i>—novel thinking I’d be reading a retelling of Mulan, which suited me just fine. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23308087.Flame_in_the_Mist__Flame_in_the_Mist___1_" title="Flame in the Mist (Flame in the Mist, #1) by Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">Flame in the Mist</a> <b>is not a fairytale</b>, however beautifully it is written. Mariko and Mulan are both intelligent women who gain strength and fierceness along their respective journeys. <br /><br />But Mariko never goes to war—she is recruited by the dangerous ‘‘Black Clan’’. Since that doesn’t happen, she never falls in love with a captain. Plus, she doesn't fit the criteria of Disney princesses. <br /><br />Oh, no. Mariko is done with dresses and pampering for ever. She wants revenge. The Black Clan tried to kill her? Well, they haven’t succeeded, so now it’s her turn to strike back.<br /><br />You know the peculiar spirits—i.e. the small dragon—that look after Mulan? We have something of a sort in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23308087.Flame_in_the_Mist__Flame_in_the_Mist___1_" title="Flame in the Mist (Flame in the Mist, #1) by Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">Flame in the Mist</a>. Unfortunately, Mariko does not have a sidekick. Fortunately, she isn’t completely alone. <br /><br />As you can see, this is more of a loose retelling of Mulan. Furthermore, Renée Ahdieh <b>touches on feministic issues better than Disney ever did</b>. She isn’t afraid to point out all that is wrong with the way men perceive women. <br /><br />There is romance, but <b>it’s not a romantic story</b>. Mariko is serious about her plan to murder the leader of the clan. At the same time, she is human—<i>her emotions sometimes get in the way.</i><br /><br />I absolutely cannot wait to see where this is all going. <b>I am in love.</b><br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16794123621413333491" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1723591814" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1723591814" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1723591814?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1723591814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15908780096746014622"><b>“You do have a flair for the dramatic.”</b><br/><br/>•Although <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18798983.The_Wrath_and_the_Dawn__The_Wrath_and_the_Dawn___1_' title='The Wrath and the Dawn (The Wrath and the Dawn, #1) by Renée Ahdieh' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Wrath & the Dawn</a>
</i> definitely did <i>not</i> make it into my all-time favourites list, the idea of giving a try to <i>Flame in the Mist</i>, inspired by <b>Disney's <i>Mulan</i> </b>(maybe the Disney movie I adore the most) and set in feudal Japan, still filled me with excitement. Sadly, however, I found that Ahdieh made once again many of the mistakes she'd made in her previous duology as well, and generally I noticed no, or very little, improvement. So let's see what</span>
  <span id="freeText15908780096746014622" style="display:none"><b>“You do have a flair for the dramatic.”</b><br /><br />•Although <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18798983.The_Wrath_and_the_Dawn__The_Wrath_and_the_Dawn___1_" title="The Wrath and the Dawn (The Wrath and the Dawn, #1) by Renée Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wrath &amp; the Dawn</a>
</i> definitely did <i>not</i> make it into my all-time favourites list, the idea of giving a try to <i>Flame in the Mist</i>, inspired by <b>Disney's <i>Mulan</i> </b>(maybe the Disney movie I adore the most) and set in feudal Japan, still filled me with excitement. Sadly, however, I found that Ahdieh made once again many of the mistakes she'd made in her previous duology as well, and generally I noticed no, or very little, improvement. So let's see what we've got here.<br /><br />•I truly must be a very strange person, because <b>I firmly believe Ahdieh's much-loved and much-vaunted writing to be the main problem</b>. As I said in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1626792970" rel="nofollow noopener">my review of <i>The Rose &amp; the Dagger</i></a>, Ahdieh tries so hard to be and sound poetical and melodious, that ultimately her narration can only come off as pretentiously high-sounding. I'm not referring to the little details, such as her choice of words and expressions, and if you take her sentences one by one, rest assured you'll find nothing wrong with them. It is when you put them all together, one after the other, when you read the book (but to get a clear enough idea even just one chapter will do) that they start feeling odd: <b>absurdly overdramatic</b> and <b>inflated to a fault</b>. I would find it boring and annoying even if it lasted for no more than a couple of pages, but here we have a whole book written like this from cover to cover, and I'll be honest, it's tiring -no, it's <b><i>exhausting</i>.</b> It's exhausting because you're forced to be continuously on edge, to wonder what on earth is happening of such importance that the author is presenting it as if 1) the end of the world is near or 2) some character just found out the Answer to the Ultimate Question of Life, the Universe, and Everything.<br />➔ <u>Practical made-up example of how even the most inconsequential events and facts have to be written according to Ahdieh</u>. This is how she would write—well, basically everything, according to the data I've picked up after reading all three of her books. <blockquote>Mariko glimpsed something on the ground. It glinted in the mud, the colour of burnt sugar.<br />She stopped on her tracks and leaned down a little, then some more. Closer.<br />She had to catch her breath; she picked the object up. So light.<br />So soft. She had found-<br />A leaf. <br /><i>I've found a leaf.</i></blockquote><br />When a reader stumbles upon a passage like this, he or she is led to believe the leaf is somehow functional, even fundamental, to the story. How do you think they'll feel when it becomes clear than it's actually not? The answer is, <b>like a deflated balloon</b>. And that is precisely the problem that Ahdieh's writing style creates, and which would not exist with a more sensible revision of the text: <b>it raises expectations that have no place there</b> and no hope to be fulfilled. I opted for inventing a brief example instead of selecting a quote from the book because, as I said, you won't find anything wrong on a microscopic level and nothing striking enough to make you understand what I mean that is brief enough to be quoted: it's <b>the ultimate, wider effect</b> you have to consider. And this effect is profoundly frustrating. <br /><br />•My second complaint concerns the logic behind some of <b>Mariko's decisions</b>. Take the first one: she doesn't want dishonour to befall her family, so she runs into the woods to understand who is after her, even though one of the problems to returning home was "the question of [her] virtue" that would be raised by her being "lost in the forest, alone with murderers and thieves" for even a couple of hours. How is spending <i>more</i> hours is there going to help in saving her family's honour, that's beyond me. You see, the thing is, <b>her choices sometimes are even the right ones, but her mental processes are all messed up</b>. She gave me never-ending headaches. <br />Another instance of how her reasoning just doesn't stand up is, why does she never once <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[wonder, at the end, about Ranmaru turning into a wolf? Shouldn't she find that strange? Or what the heck was the creature that warned her in the forest? The strangest magical things can happen and she wouldn't give it more than a passing thought <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Odd.<br /><br />•<b>Show-don't-tell who?</b> There are few things I hate more that when authors don't follow this rule. We are told-and told-and <i>told</i> Mariko is so clever and curious and always outsmarts everyone, but if you had to count the times that actually happens you wouldn't get past... one, as far as I'm concerned. Moreover, <b>Mariko stands out for being the inventor of the <i>shuriken</i>, of the grenade and of the smoke grenade. Okay... </b><br />In other words, she is so magnificent and clever, I just decided I'll call her Mary Sue 2.0. Because, you know, you can't not give a bonus point to the inventor of the <i>shuriken</i>.<br /><br />•<b>In many respects, <i>Flame in the Mist</i> is awfully similar to <i>The Wrath &amp; the Dawn</i></b>. Never mind the setting; I'm talking about more substantial elements. See if this rings a bell: <blockquote>“And a part of her couldn’t help but think—were he another boy, in another time, in another place—Mariko would have liked to hear Ōkami’s laughter.<br />Would have enjoyed being the cause of it.<br />But he was a member of the Black Clan. The band of mercenaries who had tried to kill her. Who had slaughtered Chiyo and Nobutada.<br />She hated this boy and all he stood for.”</blockquote> <br /><i>Sigh</i>. Yes. I know. <br />I would have liked some <i>meaningful</i> variation on the theme, just saying. And instead the dynamics of the romance are comparable, up to a measure, to those in TWATD, and Mariko and Shazi have much in common as well, even though the author <i>does</i> try to differentiate them by portraying Mariko as more hesitant and insecure at the beginning. Since I didn't like Shazi, you understand why I wasn't able to empathize with Mariko either. <br /><br />•Like in TWATD, there is <b>magic playing peekaboo</b> and completely devoid of contextualization: we have no clue as to what it actually is or where it comes from and it appears, like, two times in the whole book. And no one ever talks about it. Do they know it exist or do they think it's just part of the stories? Everything is so confused.<br /><br />•<b>The Black Clan</b>. Mariko keeps repeating they are terrible and cruel, but it's not as if anyone actually explains us why. Are they bandits, I suppose, since they live in the woods and all? Well, then couldn't you just say that? And did they exist before Ranmaru or did Ranmaru found them? What do they want, or what does Mariko think they want, in general, apart from killing her and all that's linked to that? Do they just rob people, normally, or what? And what have they done to deserve their reputation?<br />Reader, you will never know.<br /><br />➽ I initially rounded up my rating to three stars, but after laying out all the things I found poorly done in the book, I see I'm not being honest. I've rated three stars some books that I've enjoyed far more, and, at the end of the day,<b> I didn't enjoy <i>Flame in the Mist</i></b>. <b>I am more than sure, however, that TWATD fans will love it</b>, so if you enjoyed that duology, take this review as a "Go for it, you're in for a treat." On the other hand, if, like me, you didn't enjoy TWATD... welcome to the black sheep club. And don't worry, you can just skip this one.<br /><br /><br /><br /><b>PRE-READING</b> <br />A book partly based on <b>Disney's <i>Mulan</i></b>... <br /><br />YES! YES!<br /><br />...written by Renee Ahdieh.<br /><br />YE-oh. Uhm, okay?<br /><br />Still totally gonna read it. <i>Mulan</i> is one of my absolute favorite animated movies. Can't wait.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15908780096746014622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1987628194" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1987628194" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1987628194?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1987628194" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14752438853206090466">Originally, I gave this book 5 stars after marathoning it in one day & loving it so much. After consideration and further discussion, I’m dropping my rating to 4 stars.<br/><br/>I did really love <i>Flame In The Mist.</i> The story was entertaining, had some thrilling scenes, and was all around really enjoyable. As always, I love Renee Adhieh’s writing. She has the most delectable prose that is unlike any other YA author out there. Once you get used to it, it’s very easy to get lost in her flowery writing style,</span>
  <span id="freeText14752438853206090466" style="display:none">Originally, I gave this book 5 stars after marathoning it in one day &amp; loving it so much. After consideration and further discussion, I’m dropping my rating to 4 stars.<br /><br />I did really love <i>Flame In The Mist.</i> The story was entertaining, had some thrilling scenes, and was all around really enjoyable. As always, I love Renee Adhieh’s writing. She has the most delectable prose that is unlike any other YA author out there. Once you get used to it, it’s very easy to get lost in her flowery writing style, and I always love that about her books.<br /><br />I really loved Mariko as a main character. I especially liked how she’s not a typical Mary Sue – she’s an inexperienced fighter and struggles through training, like you would expect someone who has lived a privileged life to do. Though that does not mean she is not a TOTAL BADASS and definitely makes her way through tough moments her own way. I think she’s an admirable character and I really enjoyed her story arc.<br /><br />Despite how much I enjoyed reading the story, I quickly realized I retained almost NOTHING about this world and where the storyline is going. Could it be because I read it so fast? Absolutely. But, this is a recurring theme with Rene Adhieh’s books for me. I love them so so much in the moment as I’m reading, and the next day I can’t remember any specific details. I don’t know if I can fully attribute that lack of retention to my fast reading because it’s happened to me with her past two books, physical and audiobook formats. I think it’s just a case of her ABSOLUTELY BEAUTIFUL WRITING STYLE not always matching up with me as a reader.<br /><br />I also wasn’t a huge fan of the romance. While I do enjoy the way the characters come to complement each other, I think their development was rushed. It felt as if there was no chemistry, and then nothing but chemistry after a certain course of events that just felt unnatural. I would have loved some more time for these characters to grow together as opposed to going from strangers/enemies to acquaintances to immediately lovers.<br /><br />I feel similarly about the magic system, it was presented to in the beginning, but the ending EXPLODED with magic. I initially went into this story expecting a fictionalized feudal Japan and came out with a bit of a fantasy headache. I felt like I didn’t have enough time to grasp how the magic system works because all of the rules/future of the magic system was super saturated in the last handful of chapters. I wish it had been more spread out so that it could have been more easily comprehendible. More magic throughout the story also would have probably sped up a few of the slower scenes.<br /><br />I also want to add a TW for suicide in the first 5 pages of the book. Given, it is a ritualistic suicide which some may view as different, but it's still very graphic and could be potentially triggering. Honestly, you could skip to page 6 or so and you would not have missed anything from the story at all.<br /><br />Despite my small critiques, I really did enjoy this story. It was fun, enjoyable and had interesting character dynamics with beautiful writing. I would recommend it, but I do think you need to be in the mood for a high fantasy with lavish writing &amp; stay really focused throughout. All in all, I’m anticipating book two!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14752438853206090466" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2074982806" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2074982806" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2074982806?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/43368694-flame-in-the-mist">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=fantasy-series">fantasy-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2074982806" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14441248899443723750"><i>”Death follows indecision, like a twisted shadow.”</i><br/><br/>As it seems 2019 has officially become the year of retellings for me! And tell you what? I actually seem to like them! *lol* I never thought that I would enjoy retellings so much, but either I made really great book decisions this year or I picked the wrong retellings before. XD There’s no way to tell which one it might be but either way it’s a win-win situation for me. ;-)<br/><br/><i>”You’re the devil, Ōkami,” he muttered harshly. <br/>The ghost boy eyed him ask</i></span>
  <span id="freeText14441248899443723750" style="display:none"><i>”Death follows indecision, like a twisted shadow.”</i><br /><br />As it seems 2019 has officially become the year of retellings for me! And tell you what? I actually seem to like them! *lol* I never thought that I would enjoy retellings so much, but either I made really great book decisions this year or I picked the wrong retellings before. XD There’s no way to tell which one it might be but either way it’s a win-win situation for me. ;-)<br /><br /><i>”You’re the devil, Ōkami,” he muttered harshly. <br />The ghost boy eyed him askance. “You would know.” A grin curled up one side of his face, rendering the scar through his lips white. “Since we both came from hell.”</i><br /><br />This said let’s get to the book now! I always loved Mulan and so it’s no surprise I instantly liked our heroine Mariko. I mean yes, she makes really stupid decisions sometimes but in general I could relate to her. I'm convinced we all make mistakes every now and then and she’s not only a very young but also a sheltered girl. Before her convoy got attacked she barely even saw the outside world and now that she’s forced to stay with the Black Clan it’s like she sees the real world for the very first time. Not everything is as white and black as everyone made her believe and even her own family shows a very different face if you see it from another perspective. <br /><br /><i>Mariko breathed deep. “Am I prisoner, or am I a servant?”<br />Ōkami paused before responding. “We choose what we are in any situation, be it a word or an idea.” With a small smile, he walked away.</i><br /><br />And here are the discussions between Ōkami and Mariko I started to love. *lol* Those two are so very different but they work somehow. At first I wasn’t entirely sure who was supposed to be her love interest because honestly, Ranmaru had me intrigued from the very first moment he appeared in the book! But the longer I continued to read, the more it became obvious who would end up with whom. ;-P I’ve to admit that I liked both male MCs but for some reason I kind of liked Ranmaru more. Haha! Don’t ask me why, I guess he just peaked my curiosity and I love a good mystery. *lol* Also the way he acted, so calm and composed… He got me thinking and that’s always a good sign! He’s every inch the leader and he does a good job of it as well. Still, I’ve to admit that Ōkami had a certain appeal too. XD<br /><br /><i>”My life has been filled with death and lies and loose women.” Ōkami pushed back a fall of black hair, meeting her gaze. Holding her there. Rapt. “I regret everything else.” He smiled, his hooded, heavy-lidded eyes brimming with mockery.</i><br /><br /><i>Ranmaru’s broad lips spread into an easy smile. “I believe the stars align so that souls can find one another. Whether they are meant to be souls in love or souls in life remains to be seen.”</i><br /><br />Seriously, those two boys couldn’t have been any more different but their friendship was amazing! They were like brothers and everyone who knows me; knows I love a good sibling rep! *lol* They might not have been family by blood but they certainly were in their hearts. ;-) Also I kind of enjoyed how everyone in the Black Clan was different and contributed a part to their community. Plus: Let’s not forget about the fantasy elements in here! The idea of the flesh eating trees gave me goose bumps and the forest that protected them was amazing! And if I’m already at it: <b>I adored the ending!!!</b> =)<br /><br /><i>”It was a mistake. All of it. For as long as she’d known him, Mariko had despised the very idea of this boy. But the truth of him? <br />The truth was not quite as simple. It was a silent entreaty. A wordless plea.”</i><br /><br /><b>Conclusion:</b><br /><br />This was such a great retelling! I mean it didn’t feel like a Mulan retelling because Ahdieh made so much more out of it, the basic points however were definitely there. ;-) Mixed up with a slow burn love story and the magical element this tale really had me captivated! I loved it from the very first chapter and I continued to love it until the end! <u>The ending though!</u> There were quite a lot of things I expected but others hit me so hard that I can’t help but be in awe of Ahdieh’s skills. XD So if you’re looking for a fast and nice read, I can totally recommend this to you. ;-)<br /><br />__________________________<br /><br />What happens when a Slytherpuff and a Gryffindor (with Slytherin traits, Gryfferin?) decide to read a book together? <br /><br />Well, they buddy read <b>“Flame in the Mist”</b>! ;-P<br />Because Mulan is awesome and if this is truly some sort of retelling, I’m so here for it. <br /><br />So let’s do this and hopefully we’ll enjoy it! <br /><br />Buddy read with this awesome <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/47528961-moony-meowpoff" rel="nofollow noopener">Slytherpuff</a>! <br />We’re sooo going to rock this! =)</span>
  <a data-text-id="14441248899443723750" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1789830971" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1789830971" />
    <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink"><img alt="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568991289p2/50044222.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1789830971?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink">Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=2017-anticipated-reads">2017-anticipated-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=recommended-fantasy">recommended-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=favorite-heroines">favorite-heroines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1789830971" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15811993619717235644"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"The only power any man has over you is the power you give him." </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><br/>Holy guacamole. This was wonderful.<br/><br/>HOW COME NO ONE TOLD ME THIS IS A SERIES AHHHHHH. I WAS NOT PREPARED....<br/><br/>Alright. I wasn't that into the first 30-40%. It wasn't bad at all, but I just wasn't really connecting. Mariko is on the way to her betrothed (the prince) when she gets attacked by who she believes is the Black Clan. She manages to escape (as told by the synopsis), but she refuses to return home and tell of her su</span>
  <span id="freeText15811993619717235644" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"The only power any man has over you is the power you give him." </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />Holy guacamole. This was wonderful.<br /><br />HOW COME NO ONE TOLD ME THIS IS A SERIES AHHHHHH. I WAS NOT PREPARED....<br /><br />Alright. I wasn't that into the first 30-40%. It wasn't bad at all, but I just wasn't really connecting. Mariko is on the way to her betrothed (the prince) when she gets attacked by who she believes is the Black Clan. She manages to escape (as told by the synopsis), but she refuses to return home and tell of her survival until she can figure out who paid the Black Clan to kill her. So, she infiltrates their camp and attempts to gain their trust. <br /><br />Mariko has quite the aversion to men, being that men predominately rule in their society and women are left to please men. I totally get that, and Mariko was justified in feeling that way, but she does bring it up quite a lot. Almost too much, but whatever.<br /><br />Anyway, about half way through, once we're into the Black Clan hideout, things start to get interesting. And they just keep getting better and better. I literally could not put it down past the 70% mark. Like holy wowza... SO GOOD. It was non stop, action packed, with so many fun turns. AND THE END AHHHHH WHAT DO I DO NOW?!?!<br /><br />I TOTALLY GUESSED THE TWIST TOO. And I don't even care that I guessed it because it was so great. I was actually hoping I was right because just.. yes. So good. <br /><br />Some of the highlights for me were:<br /><br />1. Japanese inspired culture. Lush and gorgeous.<br />2. Okami. And he the fact that he has long hair.<br />3. Topknots.<br />4. The scene where Mariko falls from the... cliff thing.<br />5. Gorgeous quotes, like the following...<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"A blossom can split through a rock, given enough time."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />I did have a few small complaints - one being the magic system. It was really confusing and not really explained at all - no rules were mentioned and it seemed very random. I'm assuming this will be explained much more in the next book, but it was odd to me that it was so sporadic. <br /><br />The only other thing was the writing- not that it was bad. It just felt a bit dry and hard to follow at times. I felt the same way about Ahdieh's other series too - 'The Wrath and the Dawn'. Whatever, the story here is amazing.<br /><br />All in all, I totally recommend this. I'd read it again in a heartbeat. <br /><br /><a href="http://www.herbookishthings.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> ~ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/reverieandink/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ~ <a href="https://twitter.com/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ~ <a href="https://www.etsy.com/shop/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Etsy</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15811993619717235644" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1728997898?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1728997898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8681500517139220090"><b>So, let's get down to business.<br/><s>To defeat the Huns</s></b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1505574365ra/23937343.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“In the beginning, there were two suns and two moons.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/>In the feudal empire of Wa, a land humming legends of samurai and mythical demons hunting the woods, a woman's place is to obey her father, and later her husband, with no control over her future. Hattori Mariko, though, disagrees. Her curiosity is never satisfied and she questions, studies and learns, earning the reproach of her family, who, in an attempt to gain political favor, o</span>
  <span id="freeText8681500517139220090" style="display:none"><b>So, let's get down to business.<br><s>To defeat the Huns</s></b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1505574365ra/23937343.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“In the beginning, there were two suns and two moons.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>In the feudal empire of Wa, a land humming legends of samurai and mythical demons hunting the woods, a woman's place is to obey her father, and later her husband, with no control over her future. Hattori Mariko, though, disagrees. Her curiosity is never satisfied and she questions, studies and learns, earning the reproach of her family, who, in an attempt to gain political favor, offers her as the bride of the emperor's son, trading her like merchandise. But the old gods have different plans, and when her convoy is attacked by the infamous Black Clan, a band of thieves and mercenaries, Mariko decides to pose as a boy and infiltrate their ranks, in order to discover who paid them to murder her before she destroys them, while her twin brother is frantically searching for her. What Mariko doesn't expect is the kinship she feels towards the Black Clan, their cunning yer straightforward leader and his best friend, the Wolf with the many secrets and the layers of indiferrence to cover them. Torn between her duty to her family and her loyalty to her new home, Mariko soon realizes that there are greater forces in play, and somehow an odd girl is in the middle of the storm.<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Rise from the ashes. And take your righteous place.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>As you can tell, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23308087.Flame_in_the_Mist__Flame_in_the_Mist___1_" title="Flame in the Mist (Flame in the Mist, #1) by Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">Flame in the Mist</a> is a <b>Mulan retelling</b>, and since Mulan is one of my favorite Disney movies, not reading it was not an option. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4600197.Renee_Ahdieh" title="Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">Renee Ahdieh</a> with her unparalleled talent wove intricately the empire of Wa, <b>its lores and traditions inspired by medieval Japan</b>, and her descriptions brought the pages to life; you experienced every smell and sound, you wanted to relish every dish and wear colourful kimonos, wield a katana and fight alongside black-clad boys thirsty for revenge and justice. The writing was <b>lyrical</b>, provoking a sweet melancholy that settled in your bones. The depiction of the code of honor and morals, and the struggle to abide by them were tangible. But, as discrepant as it may sound, <b>there was something missing</b>. Perhaps that restless and insatiable feeling is connected with the repetition of phrases and inner monologues. Perhaps it had to do with the characters, and the nagging thought that they needed more development. <b>But the truth is that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23308087.Flame_in_the_Mist__Flame_in_the_Mist___1_" title="Flame in the Mist (Flame in the Mist, #1) by Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">Flame in the Mist</a>, while it ignited a spark of magic, it didn't engulf me in flames.</b><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Be as swift as the wind. As silent as the forest. As fierce as the fire. As unshakable as the mountain. And you can do anything.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>Mariko was a bit bland character. I admired her determination to matter, to survive and prove her value, but such determination could be tedious at times. She was smart and resourceful, but her lapses of judgement could turn fatal, and cause tragedies. I was more invested in the stories of the secondary characters, their ties to the fallen samurai and their plans to unravel their enemies, but I wanted something more. More time inside their head. More information about their past, and the betrayals that marked them. As for the romance?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1458811078ra/18532396.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>To be honest, I rooted for a different love interest and that's the main reason it took me some time to digest the blooming relationship between Mariko and a certain character. There was poetry in their interactions, though, and bittersweet longing coated in lies and deceipt, and it eventually managed to warm my heart.<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“The entire time she'd watched him - waited for him to join her, even in death - her features had remained serene. A flame in the mist.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><b>Why 4 stars, then?</b><br>Well, it's actually 3.5, and I did enjoy the book. It was <b>beautiful</b>, and the plot managed to captivate me until the final page, and the last chapters with their explosive twists fueled my hunger, my need to know what happens next. The way I see it, <b>I possibly had very high expectations because I am familiar with the work of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4600197.Renee_Ahdieh" title="Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">Renee Ahdieh</a>, and while I wasn't disappointed, I wasn't blown away either. </b><br><br><b>
  <i>You can find <a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/8-kat-reviews/800-flameinthemist" rel="nofollow noopener">this review</a> and more on <a href="http://booknest.eu/" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest</a>!</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8681500517139220090" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9043934509346433334" style="display:none">I knew it wasn't a good idea to read this book because I was told this is similar to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18798983.The_Wrath_and_the_Dawn__The_Wrath_and_the_Dawn___1_" title="The Wrath and the Dawn (The Wrath and the Dawn, #1) by Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wrath and the Dawn</a> and *surprise* I wasn't a fan of that duology. <br><br>Reading this book felt like waiting for math class to just fuckign <i>end.</i> I couldn't wait to get this book over. I was literally counting down the pages till this fucking ended. I. JUST. WANTED. THIS. TO. END. <br><br><b>I finally learned true human suffering.</b> <br><br>This actually wasn't that bad in the beginning except for Mariko's constant repetition of "I am brave and I won't be weak" like every two pages and the fact that the plot and romance were utter <i>shit.</i><br><br>If I can go back in time to stop myself from reading, <b>Iwould, in a heartbeat</b> because ew, this was horrible. <br><br><b>※So what is this book about???</b><br>Mariko is a daughter of a samurai who is betrothed to the emperors son. While traveling to meet him, her carriage is attacked and everyone is killed by The Black Clan. But she survives!!!!! wow, oh my god!!! Instead of going to back to her family, she decides to disguise herself as a boy and hunt the Black Clan to plot her revenge and earn her honor!!<br><br>Sounds like a great idea!!!! <b>If only it stayed as an amazing idea and not destroyed by being published in the form of this book!!!!</b><br><br>●First of all my dudes, Mariko was just fucking annoying. I get she wants to show her mama raised no coward, but like???? constantly repeating that shit for the first 50 or something pages, <b>gets really annoying.</b><br><br>Hmmmm here's something wild, shut the fuck your mouth, glue that shit shut my dude, and actually <i>do</i> something that proves your bravery!!!<br><br>※Is the Black Clan supposed to be terrifying and "so bad" enough to make me piss my pants because ummmmm, I felt like I was reading about little kids trying to play warrior. I'm????? so confused???? And it's not even the kind you want to ship, I want this romance to <i>die</i> because it's fucking cringe. <br><br><blockquote>Overall, I'm not impressed and just want my time back that was spent reading this trash.</blockquote><br><br>And a 10000000x better book about Japanese mythology is definitely <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31829155.Red_Winter__Red_Winter_Trilogy___1_" title="Red Winter (Red Winter Trilogy, #1) by Annette Marie" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Winter</a>. I totally recommend that book over this!!!!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8242705097763983279">you know that feeling when you finish a book and just have to take a moment to appreciate that it was exactly what you needed to read at that particular moment? that is what im feeling right now. i feel so content. <br/><br/>i loved everything about this. the writing was classic ahdieh - stunning and poetic.<br/><br/>the characters, especially mariko, were so real. wow. i loved mariko. she was the embodiment of a strong female. i loved the lessons she learned - how to not only accept her place as a woman, but the s</span>
  <span id="freeText8242705097763983279" style="display:none">you know that feeling when you finish a book and just have to take a moment to appreciate that it was exactly what you needed to read at that particular moment? that is what im feeling right now. i feel so content. <br /><br />i loved everything about this. the writing was classic ahdieh - stunning and poetic.<br /><br />the characters, especially mariko, were so real. wow. i loved mariko. she was the embodiment of a strong female. i loved the lessons she learned - how to not only accept her place as a woman, but the strength and power she holds because of it. <br /><br />i really enjoyed the plot. i know many people have compared this to mulan, and although there are some similarities, i wouldnt really consider this a retelling. this was its own unique story. i also loved the japanese culture and traditions present in this - it gave the story such a rich feel. <br /><br />everything about this created such a remarkable and magical book. im so happy i waited to read this until the sequel was released, because i am desperate to continue the story!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars</i></b></span>

    <a title="mxa ☂︎" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36873117-mxa"><img alt="mxa ☂︎" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595455725p2/36873117.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36873117-mxa?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36873117-mxa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36873117-mxa?shelf=2017-releases">2017-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36873117-mxa?shelf=no-nono">no-nono</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1959829677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8798107148713492726"><i>“The entire time she'd watched him - waited for him to join her, even in death - her features had remained serene. A flame in the mist.”</i><br/><br/>After reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18798983.The_Wrath_and_the_Dawn__The_Wrath_and_the_Dawn___1_' title='The Wrath and the Dawn (The Wrath and the Dawn, #1) by Renee Ahdieh' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Wrath & the Dawn</a> duology, Renee Ahdieh easily landed as one of my favorite authors. So it pains me to say that her most recent release (with the most stunning cover ever) just didn’t make the cut for me. For those who are aware of the premise, Flame in the Mist sounds pretty darn fantastic. <b>It seems like a Mulan retelling with badass warriors, </b></span>
  <span id="freeText8798107148713492726" style="display:none"><i>“The entire time she'd watched him - waited for him to join her, even in death - her features had remained serene. A flame in the mist.”</i><br /><br />After reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18798983.The_Wrath_and_the_Dawn__The_Wrath_and_the_Dawn___1_" title="The Wrath and the Dawn (The Wrath and the Dawn, #1) by Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wrath &amp; the Dawn</a> duology, Renee Ahdieh easily landed as one of my favorite authors. So it pains me to say that her most recent release (with the most stunning cover ever) just didn’t make the cut for me. For those who are aware of the premise, Flame in the Mist sounds pretty darn fantastic. <b>It seems like a Mulan retelling with badass warriors, magic, sweet revenge and action.</b> What I got instead was the main character, Mariko, wasting her days within the confinement of her thoughts and not doing <i>anything</i> significant all throughout. Also, it's definitely <b>NOT</b> a Mulan retelling as the story takes place in Japan and war is set only at the very end of the book. <br /><br /><i>Pg 58: “Anger was a reckless emotion. And she needed all her wits if she intended to outmatch this boy.”<br />Pg 73: “This boy deserved to be hung upside down and drowned in Yedo Bay.”<br />Pg 121: “Today her thoughts were consumed by murderous retribution. Mariko had dreamed of setting fire to the Black Clan’s camp no less than ten times in the past hour.”<br />Pg 131: “Mariko needed to learn why the Black Clan had brought her to their encampment.”<br />Pg 169: “I will not yield to my emotions.”<br />Pg 228: “Mariko would kill Okami if he so much as reached for a sword.”<br />Pg 240: “There was far more to the Black Clan than she’d first thought.”<br />Pg 275: “Mariko was here on a mission. Here to discover why the Black Clan had tried to kill her. To discover who wanted her dead.”<br />Pg 352: “If there was any chance of finding the Black Clan’s encampment without stumbling into a trap, Mariko hoped a girl would be the first one to do it.”</i> <br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE WRITING:</u>
</b><br />Just like in TWatD, the writing in FitM is whimsical and has a way of making you feel like you’re a part of its world. Unlike the author’s previous work, it was a strain to keep me locked in. Less than halfway through, I no longer felt the need to care for this world and its characters. <b>Seeing that all I had been able to gather were <i>overpowering</i> descriptions of unnecessary things, unexplained magical system, no character depth, boring dialogues, and lack of action.</b> Not to also mention, new characters popping in and out of the blue. I was left utterly confused by its complexity. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE CHARACTERS:</u>
</b><br /><b>Mariko:</b><br />⁃	Annoying<br />⁃	Annoyingly cocky<br />⁃	A dum dum<br />⁃	Creator of one too many unnecessary mess<br />⁃	Doesn’t clean up her mess<br />⁃	Annoying<br />⁃	Very exhausting to be in her head<br />⁃	Annoyingly stubborn<br />⁃	Hates being a girl<br />⁃	Hates being a boy<br />⁃	Annoyingly unsatisfied with her life<br /><br /><i>Pg 53: “Curious has been the word most often ascribed to her when she was younger. She’d been the watchful sort of child. The one conscious of every mistake.”<br />Pg 68: “Mariko was . . . odd. Curious. Clever. Perhaps too clever, as her father always said. It has never been met as a compliment, though she had always taken it as one… These men would not want to see Mariko as odd or curious or clever.”<br />Pg 82: “His sister had always been a scholar of reason, devoid of emotion.”</i><br /><br /><br /><b>Kenshin (Mariko’s brother):</b><br />⁃	He’s alright I guess<br />⁃	Smart unlike his sister<br />⁃	The last 150 pages left me all confused<br /><br /><b>Black Clan Members:</b><br />⁃	They didn’t annoy me <br />⁃	But they warmed up to Mariko?? so <s>SCREW YOU GUYS</s>.<br /><br /><b>Other characters:</b><br />⁃	I don’t know any of their names<br />⁃	I don’t care for them<br />⁃	What’s with their random appearances?<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE ROMANCE:</u>
</b><br />This book could do without romance. The chemistry between the characters that shall not be named was completely off. The part where they both realized their feelings for each other had me laughing and not in a good way. Their relationship is yet another thing to dwell on especially because it seemed unfocused but at the same time, the consequences towards the end says otherwise. <br /><br /><b>Le example of their love:</b><br /><i>Boy: You’re lying.<br />Girl: You’re lying too.<br />Boy: You’re a liar.<br />Girl: Take off your mask.<br />Boy: A mask can easily be taken off.<br />Girl: So you don’t mind me lying?<br />Boy: I like you less when you’re lying.</i><br /><br /><i>”I may lie every day of my life, Hattori Mariko. But my heart will always be true.”</i><br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE ENDING:</u>
</b><br /><i>huhhh????</i><br /><br /><b>
  <u>OVERALL:</u>
</b><br />Regardless of this book not living up to its potential, the writing’s gorgeous and there was some level of <i>excitement</i> with the whole random pop ups here and there. As for the romance, it’s a shame that one work’s strength turned out to be this one’s weakness (be it intentionally or not). <s>Lastly, the ending made me seriously regret reading around 400 pages because it was just pointless?</s><br />Nevertheless, I adore the author and I can’t wait to read whatever she comes up with next :)<br /><br /><b>1.75? stars</b><br /><br />---<br /><br /><s>YO, I'M SO EXCITED FOR <b>THIS</b>!</s><br />BUDDY READ WITH THE GANGSTERS???<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/42163117-emma" rel="nofollow noopener">EMMAAAAAA</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/46651661-solomon-the-bookish-king" rel="nofollow noopener">SOLOMONNNNNN</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435-elise-the-bookish-actress" rel="nofollow noopener">ELISEEEEEEEE</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8798107148713492726" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

I loved everything she stood for, determined on destroying patriarchy and finding a voice for herself. <br /><br />There's a lot of groundwork that has been set up in order for the story to be built upon and develop in the next book and it makes me so damn excited to see where it's headed! 😍</span>
