<div id="review_1767854670" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1767854670" />
    <a title="emi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34410191-emi"><img alt="emi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603747413p2/34410191.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1767854670?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emi" href="/user/show/34410191-emi">emi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=girls-kicking-ass">girls-kicking-ass</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=cover-porn">cover-porn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=i-spent-my-money-on-this">i-spent-my-money-on-this</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1767854670" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16346305959656075137"><i> 4/5 stars<br/><br/><blockquote> <b> "Be as swift as the wind. As silent as the forest. As fierce as the fire. As unshakable as the mountain." </b></blockquote></i>  <br/><br/>You might be saying to yourself, “Wow? A review for Mist in the Flame? Didn’t you promise to post this three weeks ago?” <s> Actually, you aren’t, but I’m going to pretend you actually care and are. </s> Which I reply to you. Yes. I was. But I got lazy. It happens. But better late than never. <br/><br/>First just a huge thank you for Penguin Teen sending me an arc of this book. You guys are the</span>
  <span id="freeText16346305959656075137" style="display:none"><i> 4/5 stars<br /><br /><blockquote> <b> "Be as swift as the wind. As silent as the forest. As fierce as the fire. As unshakable as the mountain." </b></blockquote></i>  <br /><br />You might be saying to yourself, “Wow? A review for Mist in the Flame? Didn’t you promise to post this three weeks ago?” <s> Actually, you aren’t, but I’m going to pretend you actually care and are. </s> Which I reply to you. Yes. I was. But I got lazy. It happens. But better late than never. <br /><br />First just a huge thank you for Penguin Teen sending me an arc of this book. You guys are the coolest. If there’s any other arc you wanna send my way, please don’t hold back. <br /><br />So now that I got all that out of the way. I just wanna say that this review isn't just a review. It's also my eulogy. Because this book actually killed me. <br /><br /><blockquote> <i> R.I.P Emi<br />June 1998-May 2017.<br />She died doing what she loves. Crying over fictional characters. </i> </blockquote><br /><br />I've been dead for three weeks and y'all didn't even notice. <s> Rude.</s> But I'm gonna forgive you if you pick up this book and join me here in the afterlife. <br /><br />This book is just so awesome? It makes me wanna run into the forest and join a group outlaws. Do they even exist anymore? Do they accept emotionally unstable introverts? If you like action, beautiful covers, girls who are better than you, and some other stuff, this book is just what you are looking for. It's also really informational? Before reading this, all I knew about Samurai is pretty much nothing and I learned so much about their history. obviously, I will never be an expert, but it's nice to read about a topic that isn't taught in schools very often. <br /><br />The writing is also so beautiful. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4600197.Renee_Ahdieh" title="Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">Renee Ahdieh</a> is establishing herself as a very consistent author which is great and all but she's also incredibly gorgeous so I'm very much intimidated by her entire life. <i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18798983.The_Wrath___the_Dawn__The_Wrath___the_Dawn___1_" title="The Wrath &amp; the Dawn (The Wrath &amp; the Dawn, #1) by Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wrath &amp; the Dawn</a> </i> is still higher on my favorites list then this one, but this was a great follow-up to that series. <br /><br />So if you didn't know what this book is about. It's marketed as a Mulan meets 47 Ronin. I am unfamiliar on 47 Ronin, so I don't know how accurate that is. But the Mulan part. It's a pretty good comparison. However, if you are going into this book expecting the entire plot of Mulan conveyed using the English alphabet and paper, you are wrong. It's there, but this book is its own separate entity. <br /><br />At the beginning of this book, Mariko, who's father is this big bad Samurai, is being sent off to marry some dude she doesn't love. Pretty stereotypical. But when she was traveling to go get married off, her party is attacked and everyone dies. But she manages to get away. Mariko figures that this group called the Black Clan was responsible because they wanted to kill her. So, instead of running the opposite direction like <i> any </i> sane person would, she disguises herself as a boy and goes undercover in the Black Clan to figure out why the hell they wanted to assassinate her.<br /><br />I'll be honest. The first part of this book is kinda slow. There is just a lot of haning around, not doing much in the woods. But once you prevail into the last part, everything becomes worth it. <br /><br />Let's talk characters. Shall we? It's been awhile since I finished this book, so I don't remember too many details. But I'll try. <br /><br /><b> Markio. </b> Can I be her? I want to be her. She's better than you. My only complaint is that she's supposed to be like this mastermind with scientific stuff, but we don't get to see that a lot. <br /><br /><b> Okami. </b> I wasn't paying any attention to his character, to be honest. I didn't think he would be important. Then Ahdieh went in a direction I didn't expect with him and I regretted barely giving him a second glance. Don't be me. Appreciate him throughout the entire novel. <br /><br /><b> Ranmaru. </b> I'm gonna be honest with you. I kinda don't remember his character very much? He reminded me of Robin Hood though. <br /><br /><b> Kenshin. </b> He's Markio brother and he's kind of an asshole. But I'm not really surprised. But I did really love how much he loved his sister? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ But would your brother work as hard as he did to find you? He set the brotherly love bar really high. I'm thinking about disappearing to see if mine would. He probably wouldn't even know I was gone.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />In conclusion. This book is amazing and you should read it. Honestly, I don't know how you are reading this and just ignoring the beautiful cover. <s> Except, is it a peacock or a phoenix on the cover? I just can't figure it out. </s></span>
  <a data-text-id="16346305959656075137" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1952315775" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1952315775" />
    <a title="Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader"><img alt="Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579173421p2/43850323.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1952315775?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★" href="/user/show/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader">Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=broke-my-heart-in-half">broke-my-heart-in-half</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=live-up-my-expectation">live-up-my-expectation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=i-love-the-cover">i-love-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=heroines-i-can-relate-to">heroines-i-can-relate-to</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=warm-my-heart">warm-my-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=enemies-to-lovers">enemies-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=i-cried-over-you">i-cried-over-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=my-book-bestfriends">my-book-bestfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=slow-burn-romance">slow-burn-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=reread">reread</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1952315775" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4283864018505330275"><b>
  <i>EDIT : I reread this book and I still enjoyed it but not as much as the first time I read it. I used to give it 5 stars but I changed my mind and gave it 4 stars instead. </i>
</b><br/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><br/>"If I am marching to my death, then I <br/>will march to it as a girl. Without fear."<br/></i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br/><br/>This book is about a girl named Hattori Mariko, whose convoy is attacked by the Black Clan, when she is on her way to the palace to meet her future husband, the future husband she does not choose and love. She is supposed to be dead</span>
  <span id="freeText4283864018505330275" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>EDIT : I reread this book and I still enjoyed it but not as much as the first time I read it. I used to give it 5 stars but I changed my mind and gave it 4 stars instead. </i>
</b><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><br>"If I am marching to my death, then I <br>will march to it as a girl. Without fear."<br></i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br><br>This book is about a girl named Hattori Mariko, whose convoy is attacked by the Black Clan, when she is on her way to the palace to meet her future husband, the future husband she does not choose and love. She is supposed to be dead but she survives and now, she wants revenge. She dresses as a boy and then she wants to find out who sent the Black Clan to kill her and why this person wants her dead.<br><br><b>
  <u>My Opinion</u>
</b><br><br>OH MY GOD. I didn't expect this. I didn't expect I would love it this much. I didn't expect the pain that I would suffer when I finished reading it. I swear, I thought about this book a whole night, last night, because I just couldn't forget how amazing it was and how it caused me a great pain. I shed tears several times over the beautiful and powerful quotes in this book. The quotes are both beautiful, powerful and great at the same time and I found myself nodding and agreeing to these quotes. There are so many quotes that I love in this book and my copy is full of sticky notes. These are one of the quotes that I love : <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><br>"There is such strength in being a woman. But it is a strength<br>you must choose for yourself. No one can choose it for you. <br>We can bend the wind to our ear if we would only try."<br></i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><br> Fear kept her alert. She would always let it feed her. Never<br>let it consume her. <br></i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>and there are still so many more quotes that I love so much that I won't put them here, because you need to read the book to see these quotes. But believe me, the quotes are so beautiful and powerful. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518605204ra/25058039.gif" width="250" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>The Plot</u>
</b><br><br>I LOVED THE PLOT. Honestly, I can't decide whether it's slow-paced or fast-paced. I mean, there are many things that happen in the book but when I finished the book, I felt it was so fast. But I also think it's slow-paced because I got the chance to know the secondary characters and the MC. Sorry if I'm being confusing hahahaha because I honestly can't decide about the pace of the book. for me, it felt both fast and slow paced. <br><br>AND THIS BOOK MADE ME LAUGH SO HARD. THAT RARELY HAPPENS. I cannot tell you the story because it might be spoiler and I don't want to spoil anyone, But I laughed several times while reading it. Most of the time, it's the banter between Mariko and Ōkami. They're just so funny and I can't help but laughing or grinning, when they bicker.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518608406ra/25058337.gif" width="250" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>
  <u>The Romance</u>
</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b><br>"My heart knows <br>your heart. A heart doesn't care about good or bad, right or <br>wrong. A heart is always true."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>I TOTALLY LOVED THE ROMANCE. THIS IS THE KIND OF ROMANCE THAT I LOVE TO READ. It is enemy-to-lover and for me, it didn't feel rushed or forced to happen. It was sweet and romantic and IT WAS SLOW BURN AND NO LOVE TRIANGLES. THIS IS THE KIND OF ROMANCE THAT I ALWAYS LOOK FOR IN BOOKS. <br><br>The MC and the love interest took time to know each other and they eventually developed feelings for each other and it happened slowly, not instantly and by the time I finished this book, I got these feelings that one day, I want to have a man that look at me and think about me the way the love interest look and think about Mariko. I just don't know what else I have to say about the romance, other than I loved it and I SHIP IT. I hope to see more of the love interest in the second book. I CANNOT WAIT TO READ IT. I HOPE THE SECOND BOOK WILL DESTROY ME. <br>I love to be destroyed by books. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518614024ra/25058804.gif" width="200" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>The Characters</u>
</b><br><br><b>*inhales* *exhales*</b> I COULD RELATE SO MUCH TO MARIKO. I swear, when I read this book and I felt like I was looking in the mirror, because I could relate to Mariko so much and Mariko was an amazing character. She was brave, fierce, strong, clever and determined. Look, even though I could relate to her very much. I wouldn't be as strong as she was. Maybe I would weep. Everything she had been through was beyond what I could bear and she was strong and fierce to deal with these problems. Honestly, I want to be just like her. <br><br>AND OH MY GOD. THE BROMANCE AND THEIR LOYALTY TO EACH OTHER. OH MY GOD. I LOVE IT SO MUCH. I CANNOT GET ENOUGH OF IT. I NEED MORE. THIS IS SO BEAUTIFUL. THIS IS WHAT I HAVE ALWAYS LOOKED FOR IN BOOKS. <br><br><b>Basically everything that I have always looked for are all in this book and I am so glad that I read it. This book is beautiful and the quotes in this book are purely beautiful and powerful. I love them so much.</b> <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><br>"I believe<br>the stars align so that souls can find one another. Whether they<br>are meant to be souls in love or souls in life remains to be seen."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br><br>✨✨✨✨✨✨✨✨✨✨✨✨✨✨✨<br><br><s>
  <b>Review to come today! All I can say now is, my heart is utterly <i>severely</i> broken.</b>
</s><br><br>----------------------------------------------<br><br><s>
  <b> I've been feeling sad and bitter for a few days because everything that I have read so far disappointed me. So I hope, it won't happen with this book. I REALLY NEED a book that leaves me in awe. </b>
</s></span>

<div id="review_2003852739" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2003852739" />
    <a title="Michiko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67899645-michiko"><img alt="Michiko" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2003852739?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michiko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michiko" href="/user/show/67899645-michiko">Michiko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2003852739" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11126730827845798408">To give you an understanding of where this review is coming from, I'm a 1st-generation Japanese-American, bisexual, and non-binary. I was really disappointed with this book. (And yes, I knew that the book wasn't really a Mulan retelling going into it, so my disappointment has nothing to do with the marketing. But the marketing <i>was</i> crap.)<br/><br/>1. There are a whole bunch of historical inaccuracies. And before you yell "But it's fantasy!" understand that this isn't an alternate Japan. It's historical Jap</span>
  <span id="freeText11126730827845798408" style="display:none">To give you an understanding of where this review is coming from, I'm a 1st-generation Japanese-American, bisexual, and non-binary. I was really disappointed with this book. (And yes, I knew that the book wasn't really a Mulan retelling going into it, so my disappointment has nothing to do with the marketing. But the marketing <i>was</i> crap.)<br /><br />1. There are a whole bunch of historical inaccuracies. And before you yell "But it's fantasy!" understand that this isn't an alternate Japan. It's historical Japan, with real historical people and places. The only thing that makes this fall under the fantasy genre is that there's a little magic thrown in, which btw Ms. Ahdieh doesn't explain at all. We don't ever learn how this magic system works, who all has magic and who doesn't, what the limits of the magic are, etc. But I'm getting off-topic. My point is, people who have no idea what they're talking about are praising this book for the historical research, and it's frustrating. Yeah Ms. Ahdieh learned some things about feudal Japan, but there's also a lot she messed up, everything from ridiculous character names to mentions of things that didn't exist in Japan until 100s of years later than when the story is set.<br /><br />2. I could happily go 20 years without reading another book involving cross-dressing written by a cis author. These books almost never consider trans/non-binary people, and keep enforcing crappy binary norms all over their novels. I'm so sick of it. If you're trans/non-binary, be aware this book has a lot of parts that might hurt you. And before you yell "But it's historical!" go do some research because trans/non-binary people have existed everywhere all throughout history. Yes the language and culture is different from how it's treated in modern Japan or modern America, but you <i>can</i> write a historical book that challenges some ideas about the notion of a gender binary.<br /><br />3. Besides trans/non-binary erasure, this book also has bi erasure. (None of Ms. Ahdieh's books have any LGBTQIAP+ characters to my knowledge, which is annoying, but that's just my personal opinion.) <i>However</i>, there's a part in this book where it makes no sense at all not to acknowledge bisexuality. This is a slight spoiler: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When the love interest boy "discovers" the cross-dressing protagonist is a girl because he accidentally sees her boobs (which btw is all sorts of problematic and harmful from a trans perspective), she kisses him literally a second later. And he kisses her back. If he thought she was a boy this whole time, and is kissing her literally a second after he sees she has boobs...that suggests he had some sort of feelings for her when he thought she was a boy, right? So he's probably somewhere on the bi spectrum? But this is <i>never</i> discussed or even mentioned once in the whole book. It's completed ignored, and this boy's bisexuality is erased.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />4. When will authors stop writing things like "tabi socks", "chai tea", etc.? Tabi <i>are</i> socks. When translated, you're basically saying "socks socks." It's obviously done to make certain westerners understand, but isn't it your job as a writer of historical fiction to convey ideas through context? You don't need to resort to this. Crap like this makes it clear the book isn't written for Japanese-Americans like me, who should be the first people you consider when writing a Japanese story in English. Related, I hate when "foreign" words are italicized in books. Especially when this is a Japanese character <i>in</i> Japan. These words aren't foreign to her, or to me. It's just another thing that tells me this book isn't written for Japanese people.<br /><br />5. I know some people call Ms. Ahdieh's books feminist, but I don't really agree. I don't know if any of them even pass the Bechdel test. This book in particular has a cast of mostly men. There's one girl who does absolutely nothing in the story except exist for the lusty male gaze of the protagonist's brother, and then <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[she dies in order to provide motivation for the brother to seek revenge. Can we please put an end to that sexist and dehumanizing trope? Please? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I can't speak for all Japanese-American/bi/non-binary people, and I understand that others might have different opinions. But I personally can't recommend this book. I'm going to go search for a book by an LGBTQIAP+ Japanese author to cleanse me of these icky, uncomfortable, and hurt feelings I got from reading this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11126730827845798408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2018240965?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=poc-interracial">poc-interracial</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=ya-ya-land">ya-ya-land</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2018240965" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13381843802920232525"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/> <br/>Did the people who read this book read a different book than the one I read? Because I did not get a romantic, action-packed adventure. I got a slow and plodding story with wooden characters and writing that was rife with purple prose. It wasn't even the fact that I went in with high expectations; despite the fact that Mulan is one of my favorite movies, I really did not like this author's other book, THE WRATH AND THE DAWN, and <i>that </i>wa</span>
  <span id="freeText13381843802920232525" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br> <br>Did the people who read this book read a different book than the one I read? Because I did not get a romantic, action-packed adventure. I got a slow and plodding story with wooden characters and writing that was rife with purple prose. It wasn't even the fact that I went in with high expectations; despite the fact that Mulan is one of my favorite movies, I really did not like this author's other book, THE WRATH AND THE DAWN, and <i>that </i>was based off one of my favorite faerie tales. So I went in with extremely low expectations and somehow, FLAME IN THE MIST managed to be <i>worse </i>than TWatD. How does that happen?<br><br><br><br>Also, let's talk about the Mulan thing. I noticed people were saying that this book was a retelling of Mulan, and I wasn't sure if it was the publisher saying that or other reviewers saying that (because reviewers say a lot of things that publishers aren't and shouldn't be held responsible for), but when I went to the <a href="http://www.penguinrandomhouse.com/books/316781/flame-in-the-mist-by-renee-ahdieh/9780399171635/" rel="nofollow noopener">Penguin website</a>, they appear to be blurbing the book as "Mulan meets Throne of Glass" and the author herself appears to be citing her love of the movie as an influence in writing this book in <a href="https://www.bustle.com/articles/177389-the-wrath-and-the-dawn-author-renee-ahdieh-announces-new-duology-flame-in-the-mist" rel="nofollow noopener">this <i>Bustle </i>interview</a>. That made me give this book the side-eye, because Mulan is a legend from China and this is a book about Japan. China and Japan have totally different cultural legacies and at several points throughout history they have clashed in very unpleasant ways. It felt extraordinarily insensitive to me to brand a Chinese legend in new, Japanese packaging. To give a Western example, it would be like taking the struggles of the Scottish and rebranding them as English. <br><br><br><br><i>"Be as swift as the wind. As silent as the forest. As fierce as the fire. As unshakable as the mountain" </i>(244).<br><br><br><br>I really don't like it when I feel like I'm being pandered to. Especially when it feels culturally insensitive. I'm sure that wasn't the author's intention, but I think that sometimes people forget that Disney stories are often based off actual folklore from actual people.<br><br><br><br>FLAME IN THE MIST is about a girl named Mariko who is the daughter of a samurai. She's on her way to be married to her betrothed, but her litter and attendants are slaughtered before she can reach her destination, and Mariko herself is saved only by sheer luck. She ends up lost and wondering, and after escaping a would-be rapist, decides to disguise herself as a boy. Lucky for her (again), because Mariko ends up in the camp of the very men who she believes were trying to kill her, a group of bandits called the Black Clan. She decides that she's going to gain their trust and learn their weaknesses so she can kill them in revenge, but this being a YA novel, she falls for the ringleader.<br><br><br><br>Mariko is no Mulan. She's one of those "strong" female characters who prove their "strength" by whining about how much it sucks to be a girl. She is <i>constantly </i>shooting off her mouth, even when she shouldn't (especially when she shouldn't), and of course her would-be enemies think this is so hilarious and endearing and are won over instead of gagging her and/or throwing her off a bridge. Also, the plot is very similar to WRATH OF THE DAWN in the sense that Mariko, like Sharzad, has a lot of reason to hate the leader, but never does, at least not without conviction, and gives into her lust way too quickly. Her emotions do not feel real - it's like she has an internal switch that flips whenever it's convenient for the plot, and also, what is going on with the plot of this story? It was so slow. I skimmed, and it still felt way too long. The writing does not help. Ahdieh makes an effort to write poetically, but instead it just feels blocky and convoluted and <i>weird</i>.<br><br><br><br><i>But the egg - that simple egg - was so wonderful. So perfect.</i><br><br><i>How could anyone who would take such care to prepare a simple egg truly be bad?</i> (106)<br><br><br><br>Also, negative points for that line. Because apparently people can't be bad if they can cook eggs. <br><br><br><br>1 star</span>
  <a data-text-id="13381843802920232525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1593136503464837563" style="display:none">Renée is an auto buy for me, so after screaming, I immediately downloaded this and started it.<br /><br />I love Mariko right from the beginning. She's so smart and so strong, but she's unaware of her abilities. It was delightful to see her figure out her potential and place in the world. The members of the Black Clan are interesting and quite the enigma. I loved seeing their truths revealed.<br /><br />I did struggle with the names and that is my main complaint. Each character seemed to have several nicknames, official names and titles and they were all thrown around. Often in the same paragraph. Eventually I sort of gave up trying to keep people straight.<br /><br />The plot is a bit of a slow burn, but it's captivating. I was sucked in right from the start. The ending is enraging and satisfying and I can't even wait to see what happens next.<br /><br />**Huge thanks to GP Putnam's Sons and Edelweiss for providing the arc free of charge**</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61624004-amy?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer17714189199407675850"><i>aaaaaaaaaaaaaaahhhhhhhhhhhhhhh.</i> nothing like being let down by your most anticipated release of the year.<br/><br/>:) :) :) i'm cool. i'm chill. whatever. <br/><br/>everybody knows too much <b>salt</b> isn't healthy for your body so i'm gonna try and be rational and keep the roasting to a minimum and everything rated G and family friendly so let's go<br/><br/><b>
  <u>General Thoughts:</u>
</b><br/><br/>i mean, how do you hear "mulan retelling" and not get excited??? sure, Miss Ahdieh and I had our differences in the past, but despite that, i thought we c</span>
  <span id="freeText17714189199407675850" style="display:none"><i>aaaaaaaaaaaaaaahhhhhhhhhhhhhhh.</i> nothing like being let down by your most anticipated release of the year.<br /><br />:) :) :) i'm cool. i'm chill. whatever. <br /><br />everybody knows too much <b>salt</b> isn't healthy for your body so i'm gonna try and be rational and keep the roasting to a minimum and everything rated G and family friendly so let's go<br /><br /><b>
  <u>General Thoughts:</u>
</b><br /><br />i mean, how do you hear "mulan retelling" and not get excited??? sure, Miss Ahdieh and I had our differences in the past, but despite that, i thought we could make up just for a sec and get together to drink chamomile tea and paint each others toenails while discussing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23308087.Flame_in_the_Mist__Flame_in_the_Mist___1_" title="Flame in the Mist (Flame in the Mist, #1) by Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">flame in the mist</a>....... but no. <br /><br />what i got, was the <b>walmart version of mulan</b>. <br /><br />this book feels like it tried too hard to be something it's just <i>not</i>, and you can feel it on every page in every sentence with every <i>word</i>, like............<br /><br />everything from the romance to the plot is so god damn predictable and boring and unoriginal, i don't even know where my disappointment starts or ends.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Characters:</u>
</b><br /><br />• <b>Mariko</b><br />i just don't like her and i hope i never meet the real life version of her bc i'm 900% sure she's the type of human that causes headaches just from being <i>present</i>. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"Hattori Mariko wasn not just any girl. She was more."</i>
</blockquote><br />She was also the most annoying mc i've ever encountered in any book, ever.<br /><br />• <b>Kenshin</b><br />all i learned was that he has even worse anger issues than i have, so he's definitely somebody i don't want anything to do with, i think the fUCK not no thanks bye<br /><br />• <b>Okami</b><br />legit the only character i actually liked. what a lad.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"You are first and foremost a person. [...] If I ever say you are not permitted to do something, rest assured that the last reason I would ever say so would be because you're a girl."<br /><br />"There is such strength in being a woman. But it is a strength you must choose for yourself. No one can choose it for you."</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />i just...... love all the women-empowering little speeches he gave. mariko was always like oh no!! i'm a woman!! :((( and okami was literally like ???????????????????? so<br /><br />nothing but respect for MY president<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Romance:</u>
</b><br />this is where i'm kinda conflicted bc even tho i hate 1/2 of the pairing (mariko), i still..... semi-liked it? more or less.<br /><br />it was still very predictable tho :) <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Plot:</u>
</b><br />yeah can i get uuuuuuuuuhhhhhhhhhhh 1 original, non-predictable, exciting plot please? trying something new.<br /><br />(1) i don't see how this is a mulan retelling (2) what even was the plot either nothing was happening or everything was happening (3) 90% of the time while reading this i was just like, with all due respect, <i>what the fuck</i><br /><br />i couldn't keep any of the characters apart, i didn't know who what when what's happening who IS THIS and i couldn't bring myself to <i>care</i> about anything or anyone. <br /><br />also, at one point i was so bored i LEGIT started STUDYING instead of reading,,,,,, this is when you know the world is ending soon, folks.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Final Thoughts:</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>i can't believe i made it to the other side; reading this book felt like one of the most difficult obstacles in my life and honestly i feel like my soul left my body somewhere around the 150 pages mark</b><br /><br />so, i guess this is it. i'm gonna go meditate or something to get rid of all this negative energy i've been carrying around me while writing this review. somebody wake me up when people stOP HYPING BOOKS FOR NO REASON like jfc i don't <i>want</i> to have all these expectations.<br /><br />i'm sorry if this review offended anybody in any way, and i literally tried to get my points across as rational as possible. give me some credit.<br /><br />(also, somewhere along the lines i forgot that Capitalization actually exists and i'm sorry but by this point and time in my career on the goodreads dot com i've stopped giving fucks, sue me)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1388506108236256734"><br/>It seems I hold the unpopular opinion in regards to this book. While all my friends complain, I’m sitting here like ??? <i> it was epic, where were you???</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490714860ra/22336419.gif' width='400' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>#1 First off, the fact that Renee wrote this book is an instant 10 point. She absolutely slayed me with The Wrath and the Dawn ((I love Khalid sm, my sweet child)) and while there are many parallels that can be linked between the two books, I found this one to have such a passionate charm. <br/><br/>#2 The writing is absolutely magnificent. It’s colourful a</span>
  <span id="freeText1388506108236256734" style="display:none"><br>It seems I hold the unpopular opinion in regards to this book. While all my friends complain, I’m sitting here like ??? <i> it was epic, where were you???</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490714860ra/22336419.gif" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>#1 First off, the fact that Renee wrote this book is an instant 10 point. She absolutely slayed me with The Wrath and the Dawn ((I love Khalid sm, my sweet child)) and while there are many parallels that can be linked between the two books, I found this one to have such a passionate charm. <br><br>#2 The writing is absolutely magnificent. It’s colourful and exquisite and contains Japanese idioms that just really make it feel so so so so well developed. At first, I will admit, I found it hard to remember each and every character, since there were a lot introduced initially, but I got the hang of it and then I was burning through the book without a second thought.<br><br>#3 CAN WE PLEASE STOP CALLING OUT MARIKO, I LOVE HER OKAY. <br><br>#4 <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Okami <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> is the love of my life. Okay, okay, I know the whole romance build up was kind of sudden but who the hell cares, its beautiful and intense and heated and just I loved it so much<br><br>#5 I love how the story was build and developed over a long arc of time. We really got to see the character’s in their day-to-day lives <br><br>#6 Kenshin was one of my favs in the beginning but then he was pissing me off left and right but then Amaya was introduced and I was like FRICKEN HELL I MUST. SHIP. <br><br>#7 Lots of plot twists that had me like BOI EXPLAIN THIS IM GOING CRAZY WITH MY THEORIES <br><br>#8 I thought the book was super bada*s and I loved the whole warrior thing and it was just awesome man. <br><br>#9 I need book 2 right now please, Renee please its my last wish. <br><br>#10 THE JAPANESE CULTURE IM SO ENCHANTED <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496105337ra/22882267.gif" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i> “Be as swift as the wind. As silent as the forest. As fierce as the fire. As unshakable as the mountain. And you can do anything...” </i><br><br>4 stars!!<br><br><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><br>i'm so fricken stoked for this book, honestly, if it disappoints i will end 2017 ((also i know NOTHING about mulan PUT YOUR PITCHFORKS DOWN im going to go research the hell out of it rn))<br><br><b> <i> Buddy read </i></b> with the squad, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10502567" rel="nofollow noopener">Jia</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/42130592" rel="nofollow noopener">Charlotte</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/27713046-aaron-rourke" rel="nofollow noopener">Aaron</a> &amp; <s>fake buddy reading with</s> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/29249069" rel="nofollow noopener">Prag</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/61624004" rel="nofollow noopener">Amy</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <span id="freeText8976514964662304972" style="display:none">"Death follows indecision, like a twisted arrow." <br /><br />That quote, the world of this book in general, the Nightbeast creatures and Kenshin (Mariko's brother), were the only great things in this story.     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1723659470" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1723659470" />
    <a title="Nastassja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja"><img alt="Nastassja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596034018p2/7734134.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1723659470?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nastassja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nastassja" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja">Nastassja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Mulan retelling</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=abs-alert">abs-alert</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=excellent-writing">excellent-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=mind-blowing-cliffhanger">mind-blowing-cliffhanger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=this-girl-is-daft">this-girl-is-daft</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=3rd-pov">3rd-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=sugar-overdose">sugar-overdose</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=swoon-worthy-hero">swoon-worthy-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1723659470" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13702742829369745894"><p><i>*I received a copy of this book from the publisher in exchange for an honest review*</i><br/><b><blockquote>“I’ve never been angry to have been born a woman. There have been times I’ve been angry at how the world treats us, but I see being a woman as a challenge I must fight. Like being born under a stormy sky. Some people are lucky enough to be born on a bright summer’s day. Maybe we were born under clouds. No wind. No rain. Just a mountain of clouds we must climb each morning so that we may see the sun.”</blockquote></b><br/>I was hesitan</p></span>
  <span id="freeText13702742829369745894" style="display:none"><p><i>*I received a copy of this book from the publisher in exchange for an honest review*</i><br><b><blockquote>“I’ve never been angry to have been born a woman. There have been times I’ve been angry at how the world treats us, but I see being a woman as a challenge I must fight. Like being born under a stormy sky. Some people are lucky enough to be born on a bright summer’s day. Maybe we were born under clouds. No wind. No rain. Just a mountain of clouds we must climb each morning so that we may see the sun.”</blockquote></b><br>I was hesitant to read <i>Flame in the Mist</i> after a total miss-miss <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18798983.The_Wrath_and_the_Dawn__The_Wrath_and_the_Dawn___1_" title="The Wrath and the Dawn (The Wrath and the Dawn, #1) by Renée Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wrath &amp; the Dawn</a> was for me, so take to consideration that if you read and enjoyed the aforementioned TWATD, there's a very big chance you'll enjoy FITM as much or maybe even more.<br><br>This book follows a story of seventeen years old Mariko, whose life is suffocating her with rules and confines of being a proper lady, meant for only one purpose: to be a prize sold into a political marriage that will benefit her father. So when on her way to her future husbands, Mariko is almost killed and is presumed dead for the rest of the world, she seizes the opportunity to finally become her own person and follows her dreams. Many of you already know, this book is <b>a loose retelling of Mulan</b>, featuring a strong-minded heroine and her adventures in <i>feudal Japan</i>. Japanese culture is, alas, a rare guest in YA literature these days, and one of the reasons I was willing to give Renee Ahdieh another chance was this unique setting, and, plus, you know, who can say no to Mulan, right? I must say, to the extent of my knowledge, which is really not big, and judging by the feelings I had during the reading process, I absolutely loved the setting in this book. It really felt like I was reading a book about Japanese culture and had this ghostly feeling of being present in a world of <i>samurais and ronins</i>; I felt <i>bushido</i> – the way of the warrior - the heroine and other characters were following. <br><b>Side note:</b> <i>I would recommend to look into the glossary at the end of the book before you start reading. There's a lot of Japanese terms in the book that will make it easier if you acknowledge yourself with them beforehand.</i> <br><br><b>The first 30% or so of the book were perfect</b> for me: I liked everything about it; I admired and almost loved Mariko as our main character: her resolve to act, to rise above her stand, which was a hard task for a woman at the time, was admirable. And Mariko used her brains and wisdom to fight her way in the world of men dominance. She wasn’t perfect, she made mistakes, but imperfect is what means to be human. Funny thing, though, is <b>the more I read the more repetitive everything Mariko did became</b>. It felt like she stuck in her character development at one point, and there was nothing to show any progress, only the author’s desperate attempt to justify Mariko by telling to us how smart and sly she is, how she outsmarted everyone, and how everyone was nodding in confirmation of Mariko’s genius, but <b>'tell, don’t show' is not the best way of moving your character development</b>. Readers need facts to believe, and the book demonstrated the opposite of author’s words. For example, almost everything Mariko did when she got to the <i>Black Clan</i> (Rebels) was forgiven or oversight: Black Clan executed people for less than what Mariko was given a free pass for. And why? Because she’s a mysterious new recruit? Or because she’s so special? Special snowflake alert someone?! Or sometimes the logic behind her actions was so lame, you couldn’t understand how did this happen if even a child could’ve predicted the outcome Mariko couldn’t see <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When Mariko warned her brother about Black Clan’s plan to raid the granary, she expected what? That there wouldn’t be any fight, sworn enemies would just drink tea, talk and go home? Or after she understood how fucked up the situation was, because of her stupidity she did what? She set granary on fire expecting to do what exactly? This was the food her people needed, and she thought using bombs in the proximity of the easily inflamed granary would do what, again? Fireworks? Well, that was definitely so stupid I can’t even say how disappointed I was with Mariko. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><i><blockquote> He was smart, despite his age. Exceedingly watchful. <b>A trait Mariko prized in herself.</b>
</blockquote></i> <br>Um, no Mariko, bragging about how genius you are is a way to becoming an egotistical schmoe. <br><br>Alas, I must admit that there was not enough depth to the main character to make me fully sympathize with and respect her. <b>Secondary characters, though, they were more interesting than Mariko.</b> Remember three mysterious book boyfriends I mentioned in my updates? Yes, Okami, Kenshin and Ranmaru are their names. Though they had less book space than Mariko did, I found myself following their stories with much more interest that I did with the heroine. I don’t want to reveal who was Mariko’s love interest, because it is kind of a surprise, but I'll mention Kenshin - Mariko’s brother. <b>I was looking forward to siblings’ relationship</b>, which is one of my favorite topics in books because I have a brother and can totally relate to conflicts between siblings. Alas, in this book there wasn’t enough ground to note something remarkable about Mariko and Kenshin’s relationship. They barely share one scene, and in the whole book, there was little mentioning of their ‘before’ relationship. <b>Despite often sounding wise and telling the right thing, characters lacked some integral depth that would make them more endearing for a reader like me.</b> <br><br>The other <b>major problem I had with this book is the romance</b>. I don’t know what it is about Renee Ahdieh’s writing, but the way she outlines the romantic relationship between the main characters is very cliché-like and oppressive. What I mean is she seems to always follow the same pattern in her books: <b>from enemies to lovers</b>, where characters start strong and independent, but the more time they spend in the near proximity to their romantic interest, the clingier they become. In this book, Mariko had a solid mission. <b>Quoting:</b> <i>Follow orders. Engender trust. Strike when they least expect it.</i> She repeated these words a million times, I swear, they became some kind of parrot words. But what she actually spent her time doing? Salivating over her romantic interest’s abs. <br></p><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1398827736ra/9469366.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><p>Her trail of thoughts: I hate him, but I want him; I was always so strong-willed, but I see his abs and to what places my will goes? The love interest brought out a wild, uncontrolled part of herself, Mariko had not even known existed before. Right, that sounds alarmingly familiar. And the same goes for the aforementioned love interest: he was always so controlled and the girl made him loose control he so much prided himself for. Oookay, if you say so, darling. *redirects to the gif above* <b>I think the author rushed the romance too much, it would’ve been better if the romance was left on the stage of hints and slow-burn for the next book to develop more, because it seriously turned the whole story into one angsty drama with hasty love-for-life declarations that spoiled all the fun for me.</b><br><br>But, as it was with the romance in TWATD, I was rooting for secondary characters’ romantic developments in FITM as well. I don’t know why, but in both author’s previous books and in this one, <b>forbidden romance between secondary characters feels more real and endearing to me</b>. There wasn’t much of it, and the scenes we had were heartbreaking and sweet and ten times more intriguing than Mariko’s love drama. <br><br>One more thing I want to mention in my review is <b>the ending</b>. I am sorry to be such a Grinch, but, again, I wasn’t impressed with it, and the twist didn’t make me gasp, only if maybe in disappointment <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Okami turned out to be the true leader of the Black Clan and true heir of the Samurai legacy. Um, he was perfect before and now he became ideal for Mariko to marry and ally her family with him when he restores his birthright. And who doubts that he would? Not me. Predictable much. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b><u>Overall</u></b>, <i>Flame in the Mist</i> is <b>definitely a book worth reading if only for the Japanese setting and Eastern wisdom</b>. But if you weren’t a fan of the author’s previous works, don’t expect to fall in love with this one, because it follows a lot of the same tropes TWATD had. And, on the contrary, if you were a fan, it is highly positive you will love this book as well. <b>For me it was a 50/50 case, some things I liked a lot, some made me roll my eyes a lot.</b> But I am definitely reading book 2 (by the way, is it a duology or trilogy?), and am looking forward to more book space for my new book boyfriends and secondary romances. Also, the plot was quite engaging, and a couple of questions that are left make me highly curious as for how things will work out in the sequel. <br><br><b>My finale verdict: recommended!</b></p></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="13702742829369745894" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1533634072" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1533634072" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31923026-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533734143p2/31923026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1533634072?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/31923026-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1533634072" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5897892100899137996">This is my first book by Renee Ahdieh and it most certainly won't be my last. The writing is gorgeous, truly captivating me from start to finish. The feudal Japanese setting is fantastic and original. I have read very few books set in Japan, but I enjoyed this so much..I plan to fix that. The story is full of samurai, geisha, ronin, emperors, honor, secrets, and family. And even though at times the story was slower than I would've liked, I was enchanted through and through.<br/><br/>I read this as a buddy</span>
  <span id="freeText5897892100899137996" style="display:none">This is my first book by Renee Ahdieh and it most certainly won't be my last. The writing is gorgeous, truly captivating me from start to finish. The feudal Japanese setting is fantastic and original. I have read very few books set in Japan, but I enjoyed this so much..I plan to fix that. The story is full of samurai, geisha, ronin, emperors, honor, secrets, and family. And even though at times the story was slower than I would've liked, I was enchanted through and through.<br /><br />I read this as a buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/32342930-lauren-shakespeare-whisky" rel="nofollow noopener">Lauren</a>. She writes strong, thoughtful reviews and has excellent taste in books. Check it out :)<br /><br />Mariko is on her way to Inako to marry the emperor's son when her litter gets attacked. If the Black Clan tried to kill her, then she'll be damned if she doesn't find out why and get her revenge. So Mariko is going to infiltrate the gang and do just that. Only problem is this <b>is</b> feudal Japan. Women don't have freedom. Cue the feminist parade! So Mariko disguises herself as a boy in order to successfully attempt her plan.<br /><br />We should probably be thinking oh Mariko is so smart. She is taking care of herself. Now she did have a couple badass moments, but these were so far and few between. We kept being told how smart she is. And I mean consistently by not only Mariko but her brother Kenshin as well. I still feel we never saw this.<br /><br />Kenshin desperately wants to find his sister and rescue her. He's an excellent samurai and tracker. He actually is a badass. The love he has for his sister runs deep, but he's also a ruthless individual who will do whatever it takes. I really enjoyed his complexity. Plus that sheer determination to find his sister. Would your brother do that for you? Mine for sure would not.<br /><br />I really loved a lot of the characters actually. Okami, Amaya, Yoshi. I guess it doesn't do you any good if I just list random character names. But trust me, they are wonderful. My least favorite was Mariko even though her journey is still engrossing. I am curious how the romance is going to develop. It just peaked it's head. It feels like a lot of this book was setting things up for the future. There is political intrigue that seems like it'll be of larger importance later in the series. The complex dynamic of the royal court was certainly interesting.<br /><br />I loved the use of Japanese mythology and history throughout. I cannot speak on how accurate these are because I am not quite as familiar with the culture or history. But it is all very fascinating and it added to the excellent world building. There are several unfamiliar Japanese terms used throughout. I really enjoyed them, though it would be helpful to know you can refer to the glossary at the back of the book. I used google for a while before I realized.<br /><br />I could have used a bit of explanation on the magic system. There didn't seem to be any rhyme or reason to it. It felt very random. All this aside, I actually thoroughly enjoyed the book. The writing was exquisite with incredible world building. I loved the feminist theme throughout! The characters were wonderful. The sequel has the potential to be even better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5897892100899137996" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1878610446" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1878610446" />
    <a title="Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40997852-nicole"><img alt="Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605132719p2/40997852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1878610446?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole" href="/user/show/40997852-nicole">Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of the Wrath and the Dawn.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40997852-nicole?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40997852-nicole?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40997852-nicole?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1878610446" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18349565950653420234"><i>
  <blockquote> “I will not be bandied about by men any longer. I am not a prize to be bought or sold.” </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/><b>actual rating: 3 1/2 stars</b><br/><br/>Rating <i>Flame in the mist</i> wasn't an easy decision. At first look, it's definitely 4 stars but then you start thinking and noticing imperfections and you realize the fun alone is not enough. <br/>It had so much potential and I expected more (considering my love for Mulan & Japanese culture). <br/><p><br/>All her life, Mariko wanted to be something, more than just a noble's daughter. Life as a girl </p></span>
  <span id="freeText18349565950653420234" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote> “I will not be bandied about by men any longer. I am not a prize to be bought or sold.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><b>actual rating: 3 1/2 stars</b><br /><br />Rating <i>Flame in the mist</i> wasn't an easy decision. At first look, it's definitely 4 stars but then you start thinking and noticing imperfections and you realize the fun alone is not enough. <br />It had so much potential and I expected more (considering my love for Mulan &amp; Japanese culture). <br /><p><br />All her life, Mariko wanted to be something, more than just a noble's daughter. Life as a girl wasn't satisfying, especially now that she's betrothed to the emperor's son. <br />On her way to the capital, she escapes an ambush leaving her the only survivor. Therefore, she tries to infiltrate the Black Clan, her assassins, to discover their motives, she can't go back or she'll be a shame to her family. Dressed as a boy, she succeeds and meets Takeda Ranmaru, and his second-in-command, his best friend Okami. Soon, she discovers that the truth is way more complicated and starts questioning what she knew all her life.<br />Meanwhile, her twin Kenshin will do anything to retrieve his sister.<br /></p><p><br />I enjoyed reading Flame in the Mist a lot. It was one of my most anticipated books in 2017. I wasn't a big of the Wrath and the Dawn but come on, this is set in <b>Japan</b>. And here's the thing, I'm obsessed about Japan, especially the <b>Edo</b> period. So this is a Mulan retelling (one of my favorite Disney movies), set in the old Japan times, and with a promising summary, what's there not love?<br /></p><p><br />It doesn't stop there. While reading this book, there are so many Japanese elements I liked:<br />✓<b> Samurais.</b> I <i><b>love</b></i> Samurais (watched many anime about them) and oh, the heroine's brother is a Samurai named Kenshin. Seriously, that's so awesome.<br />✓<b> Geishassssssssss. <br />✓ Japanese words.</b> So I didn't know about the glossary until I was done (it wasn't in my copy anyway), so make sure to not forget it. At first, it was cool when I recognized many words. It stopped being cool when they became too many. But hey, we always have google.<br />✓ <b>A demonic forest</b> (with yokai, even if it's a myth, because what if it wasn't?). <br /></p><p>
  <br />
  <i>
    <b>
       “Our greatest enemy can often be found within.”
    </b>
  </i>
  <br />
</p><p><br />However, when I look more closely, I realize that no matter how much appreciate these things, it's not enough. There were many things I didn't like. At all. <s>You'll notice btw a great amount of which reminds me in this review.</s><br /></p><p><br />►<b> Mariko.</b><br />✔ She didn't annoy me (believe me, it's something). She was likable and I liked how she always wanted to be someone more than her society allowed her to.<br /><br /> ✘ She sounds so badass and smartass. That's it. <b>Sounds. </b>We are told all the time how smart she is but like everyone already said, <b>show instead of telling.</b> Eventually, we get tired of hearing what a genius she is while taking illogical decisions. So she's making these super cool weapons... to the people who tried to kill her. She claims to make them trust her. But if she's so intelligent, she'll notice that she's helping more than hurting. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And then we are told what genius she is for inventing a weapon (which is dynamite, I think?) anyway, it didn't really fascinate me. We only have a vague idea of how she came up with it but nothing more <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Don't get me wrong, I liked her but I just wanted cleverer actions on her part. Later, she starts repeating herself. We hear the same ideas all time. No, I shouldn't do that or I'll be a traitor and dozens of other similar words. It gets tiring. I also didn't understand if she can't go back because it'll be a shame, then why stay longer in the forest and try to discover your murders intentions? If she goes back, it'll be a bigger shame, right?<br /></p><p><br />► <b>The love relationship:</b><br />✔ It was so cute. I don't mind hate to love relationships no matter how cliche they are. I also liked the love interest, no, not saying his name! The tension build up was so sexy that'll make you root for them. I hoped we had even less romance, though.<br /><br />✘ It's so similar to the wrath and the dawn. The whole book is, for that matter. Sure, another setting but the events and characters are at the core the same. I should mention that I liked this more than the Wrath and the Dawn (wasn't a fan of Shazi in the first book). So I'm pretty sure the fans of her other duology will love this one. Now this one is a huge spoiler concerning the romance and the end so if you're planning on reading this book, please don't read it. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I didn't mention that Okami is the love interest because I doubted it until it was too obvious to ignore. Why? Easy, I couldn't believe Mariko will fall in love with the <i><b>second in command</b></i> and not the boss. Although I swear, I felt that the lazy boy will be the love interest from the start but it couldn't be! It's too good to be true. Why? Because for once, the heroine isn't in love with the leader. Eventually, I knew that he <i>is </i> the head of the Black Clan, I hoped my suspicions won't be confirmed but of course, they were. The end reminded of ACOMAF for some reason, kinda similar . So yeah, I was dissapointed <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /></p><p><br />► <b>The writing:</b><br />✔ It's pretty, and easy to follow. Renee painted the picture in my mind leaving a space for my own imagination.<br /><br />✘ It became too much sometimes, too many descriptions for obvious things. Even though I like the concept, we hear about the Furinkazan more than necessary (it doesn't make the book more Asian if it was repeated all the time, you know. Which is NOT even Jap). <br /></p><p><br />► <b>Her past life. </b><br />✘ So she has a brother, a twin. <b>We barely know anything about Mariko and Kenshin's relationship. </b>How he treats, for example. Yeah, sure he was always protective and stuff. But is adding few memories too much? I'd liked to know more about her relationship with her family members. She only tells us that she's mistreated because a girl but never <i>how</i>. I was disappointed when then this topic was poorly handled. I also didn't like him much. <br /></p><p><br />► <b>The secondary characters.</b><br />✔ One of the best things about this book! I liked to know more about them! Yoshi, Ren, Yumi, and everyone. It was nice to see her spending time with other people who had their own personalities, not just fillers. I also liked Kenshin and Amaya's relationship but wished more depth in his character.<br /><br />✘ So we have a name, Okami. Aka Wolf. Ironically, I read Scarlet this week and the literal meaning of the word annoyed me then. Still annoying here.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I'm including this in secondary characters because I'm not sure where else it fits. We have shapeshifters? Anyway, Mariko never once wondered about their origin even when she meets one. I found it so lacking. The fox reminded of Kurama in Yu Yu Hakusho (and the yokai too). Anyway that's why I think these people are yokai which is not a myth <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /></p><p><br />► <b>The feminist aspect</b><br />✔ I liked how even in those hard times, she was trying to prove herself and value as a woman. <br /></p><p>
  <br />
  <i>
    <b>
       “I’ve never been angry to have been born a woman. There have been times I’ve been angry at how the world treats us, but I see being a woman as a challenge I must fight. Like being born under a stormy sky. Some people are lucky enough to be born on a bright summer’s day. Maybe we were born under clouds. No wind. No rain. Just a mountain of clouds we must climb each morning so that we may see the sun.”
    </b>
  </i>
  <br />
</p><p><br />Briefly, <b> if you enjoyed TWATD, then I'm sure you'll like this one. If you didn't</b>, well, <b>I don't recommend it. </b> It doesn't end with a cliffhanger, not a major one at least. I will be reading the sequel of course, even though this book had many problems, it's still set in Japan. It was also so fun. And oh, I don't think it's a Mulan retelling, only dressing up as a boy is a common thing.<br />This book was far from being perfect and it could've been better but I liked it.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="18349565950653420234" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1723979122" class="readable"
